  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c61c5f4b-dcea-4d79-a423-4aaa2cb7f0bd'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

But the paperback bind-up (which comes with The Favor<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This is actually a novella, which means it is only available in e-format. (Like Amazon or Nook). But the paperback bind-up (which comes with The Favorite) comes out on March 3, 2015 if you would like a physical copy.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2391282155?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2391282155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14906838201324113804"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567368729i/28085330._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> </blockquote>In the main series, Queen Amberly is the epitome of <b>poise, grace and love</b>...<br/><br/>BUT back in her day, she was quite the feisty girl (well, kind of) (okok, not <i>really</i>)<br/><br/>I mean, she did <b>shock the entire world </b> when she (a lowly Four) won the Selection and was granted the honor of marrying Prince Clarkson. <br/><br/>But as far as being fiesty (or at the very least...interesting)? Nope. Nada. Zilch.<br/><br/>When we read her own story, every bit of <b>magic and love fizzled out</b> - like a firework on the fifth of July. Nothing s</span>
  <span id="freeText14906838201324113804" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567368729i/28085330._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote>In the main series, Queen Amberly is the epitome of <b>poise, grace and love</b>...<br><br>BUT back in her day, she was quite the feisty girl (well, kind of) (okok, not <i>really</i>)<br><br>I mean, she did <b>shock the entire world </b> when she (a lowly Four) won the Selection and was granted the honor of marrying Prince Clarkson. <br><br>But as far as being fiesty (or at the very least...interesting)? Nope. Nada. Zilch.<br><br>When we read her own story, every bit of <b>magic and love fizzled out</b> - like a firework on the fifth of July. Nothing special, nothing wondrous and ultimately, a bit sad. <blockquote>
  <i>For as harsh as his words were, his voice seemed to caress my name.</i>
</blockquote>It was depressing to watch this young girl so easily fall prey to the manipulative, cruel prince. When he finds out that Amberly was poisoned in her home country (air quality, etc) - <b>he recoils in horror </b> at her infertility and her diseased body. <br><br>And yet, as much of a victim Amberly is...I still <b>couldn't stand her. </b> She chose her life. She lets Clarkson be her everything right away -<b> no independent thinking,</b> no attempt to assert herself. <blockquote>
  <i>“His world looked like a storm. I was going to be its center.”</i>
</blockquote>She's chosen not for her love, or for her looks...merely because she's <b>willing to obey </b>Prince Clarkson's every whim. He swears her to secrecy? She doesn't tell a soul. He tells her to cut her hair? She lobs off nearly a foot. <br><br><b>He says to jump, and she's already jumping.</b> <blockquote>
  <i>Because if it was a choice between him or me, I didn't think I'd be able not to put him first. He was the prince, and his life was invaluable to the country. But more than that, it was invaluable to me.</i>
</blockquote><b>Thank goodness this one was short - I don't think I could've handled much more of it.</b><br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Okay, in Book 1 - Queen Amberly didn't have an accent but her sister had a strong southern twang (since they were Fours from the south). In this one, Amberly is said to be from Honduragua and has a fittingly strong native accent from that area. So, how did Amberly have a native Honduraguan accent while her sister is a southern belle? Somebody didn't plan out the audiobook too wellllllll.....<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14906838201324113804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9557364316819758516"><b>What the shit is this?</b><br/><br/>This was supposed to be a heartfelt tale of how Maxon's mom, Amberly, went on to win the Selection and become Queen. Keyword: <b>
  <i>supposed</i>
</b>.<br/><br/><b>This is not a love story; its a portrayal of an unhealthy relationship</b>. Maxon's dad (he shall hereby be referred to as M'sD as I didnt bother to remember his name and I don't care enough to check) is one of the most assholic son of a bitches I have ever read about and Amberly is not only a human doormat, but also the most naïve idiot I h</span>
  <span id="freeText9557364316819758516" style="display:none"><b>What the shit is this?</b><br /><br />This was supposed to be a heartfelt tale of how Maxon's mom, Amberly, went on to win the Selection and become Queen. Keyword: <b>
  <i>supposed</i>
</b>.<br /><br /><b>This is not a love story; its a portrayal of an unhealthy relationship</b>. Maxon's dad (he shall hereby be referred to as M'sD as I didnt bother to remember his name and I don't care enough to check) is one of the most assholic son of a bitches I have ever read about and Amberly is not only a human doormat, but also the most naïve idiot I have ever come across-<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"From now on your only job is to show up, be a lady, sit there, and smile."<br />[M'sD's mom] eyes met with mine as she ended her speech, and, stupidly, I thought that was a command. <b>So I smiled</b>. The queen was not amused...</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>Really, Amberly? <i>Really</i>?</b><br /><br />And I mean it when I say they had an unhealthy relationship comment. M'sD shrivels up his face in disgust when he hears about the deformities people get in Amberly's hometown, and makes Amberly's feel extremely shitty when she finds out that she is infertile. And Amberly, naturally, curls up in a corner, weeps about how ruined her life is now that she can't make little demons with M'sD and laments about how it's <i>all her fault</i>.<b> And I wish I was kidding, but that's exactly how it went</b>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7944060890440862220">Buddy read with my girl, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/86233338-desire-lambert' rel='nofollow noopener'>Desireé</a> :)<br/><br/><b>
  <u>4 Queen, Wife, Adore. ★'s</u>
</b> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“You will be the only thing in this world that is truly mine. And I will put you on a pedestal so high, it will be impossible for anyone not to adore you.”</i>
</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1543275640i/26652408._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This novella was surprisingly a very delightful read. I have never liked Clarkson because he was always shown as a mean hurtful tyrant and although I still don't exactly like him I got to see him through different eyes. Amberly's eyes. She is such a sweet and caring person th</span>
  <span id="freeText7944060890440862220" style="display:none">Buddy read with my girl, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/86233338-desire-lambert" rel="nofollow noopener">Desireé</a> :)<br><br><b>
  <u>4 Queen, Wife, Adore. ★'s</u>
</b> <br><br><b>
  <i>“You will be the only thing in this world that is truly mine. And I will put you on a pedestal so high, it will be impossible for anyone not to adore you.”</i>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1543275640i/26652408._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This novella was surprisingly a very delightful read. I have never liked Clarkson because he was always shown as a mean hurtful tyrant and although I still don't exactly like him I got to see him through different eyes. Amberly's eyes. She is such a sweet and caring person though if you've read all the other books then you already know this about her. I didn't love the fact that she was so damn submissive, whatever he told her to do she would jump. But whatever if it worked for them then so be it! Amberly got what shes always wanted- Clarkson and a whole new life. And Clarkson got a little peace. <br><br><b><i> “You’ve kept my secrets, and I assure you, if you marry me, there will be scores more to keep. You don’t judge me or seem startled by much. You’re soothing.”</i> His gaze traveled up to my eyes. <i>“I’m desperate for peace. I think you might be the only chance I have at that.”</i> I smiled. <i>“The center of your storm?”</i> He exhaled, looking relieved. <i>“Yes.”</i></b> <br><br>I really do believe their love for one another was genuine at least :) Overall this was really charming and such a cute short story. I loved getting a chance to see how Maxon's parents met, I just wish I knew how Clarkson went from this kind-ish boy to be such a cruel and hateful man. Everyone who loves <i>The Selection</i> should really take the time to read this. <br><br>Illustration of Queen Amberly &amp; What I picture she'd look like.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544336606i/26717771._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Illustration of King Clarkson &amp; What I picture he'd look like.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544350328i/26718323.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1543275640i/26652408._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>“It’s a strange thing to discover how much you matter to people you didn’t really know you mattered too.”</i>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1544388474ra/26720269.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>“This was joy. This was love. So many words you hear about or read about and now...now I knew them.”</i>

</a><br/><br/>The Queen is #0.4 in The Selection series by Kiera Cass. It’s no secret how much I am in love with this series. I have been from the start. This little novella explains so much as to what made King Clarkson the man we know him as. It is the story of the previous Selection, when Queen Amberly met Clarkson while he was a Prince choosing his own future bride.<br/><br/><a href='http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/gown_zps6a479b78.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413138759i/11470282.jpg' alt=' photo gown_zps6a479b78.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <br/><br/>Even though we get a good look at Clarkson’s own parents, the current King and Queen and their very dysfunctional relationship, I sti</span>
  <span id="freeText8277032831569114915" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/images5_zpsc303661c.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>The Queen is #0.4 in The Selection series by Kiera Cass. It’s no secret how much I am in love with this series. I have been from the start. This little novella explains so much as to what made King Clarkson the man we know him as. It is the story of the previous Selection, when Queen Amberly met Clarkson while he was a Prince choosing his own future bride.<br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/gown_zps6a479b78.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413138759i/11470282.jpg" alt=" photo gown_zps6a479b78.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>Even though we get a good look at Clarkson’s own parents, the current King and Queen and their very dysfunctional relationship, I still have a little trouble putting that Clarkson together with the one that so brutally beat Maxon. <br><br><b>
  <i>“This was joy. This was love. So many words you hear about or read about, and now…now I knew them.”</i>
</b><br><br>Amberly was clearly smittened with Clarkson before she even met him. But were the reasons Clarkson chose her for love, or just because she was submissive to him? <br><br><b>
  <i>“You’re soothing. I’m desperate for peace. I think you might be the only chance I have at that.”,/i&gt;</i>
</b> <br><br>The Amberly we meet, though, is every bit the poised woman and future Queen we know her as. <br><br><b>
  <i>“You will be the only thing in this world that is truly mine. And I will put you on a pedestal so high, it will be impossible for anyone not to adore you.”</i>

<div id="review_1710276412" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1710276412" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1710276412?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51318038-elena?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1710276412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer230480306686904622"><blockquote>
  <i>“You’ve kept my secrets, and I assure you, if you marry me, there will be scores more to keep. You don’t judge me, or seem startled by much. You’re soothing.” His gaze traveled up to my eyes. “I’m desperate for peace. I think you might be the only chance I have at that.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I mean, I can see why King Clarkson was an actual jerk face in The Selection. He didn't like America, and he didn't like some of the girls. I'm pretty sure he got that from his mother, but pretty sure his attitude comes from </span>
  <span id="freeText230480306686904622" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“You’ve kept my secrets, and I assure you, if you marry me, there will be scores more to keep. You don’t judge me, or seem startled by much. You’re soothing.” His gaze traveled up to my eyes. “I’m desperate for peace. I think you might be the only chance I have at that.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I mean, I can see why King Clarkson was an actual jerk face in The Selection. He didn't like America, and he didn't like some of the girls. I'm pretty sure he got that from his mother, but pretty sure his attitude comes from his father. Even though the King and Queen before Clarkson and Amberly were mentioned like once (I think) in The Selection, there wasn't much said and nothing was needed. When Clarkson was a prince, he actually seemed nice and showed that he cared about the girls just like Maxon did! The difference is that Clarkson never smiled, never tried to laugh, and only smirked or showed half a grin once or twice. But suddenly Amberly is able to bring him peace and is able to do the things he's been waiting for: <b>keep his secrets, bring him peace, and not act like a spoiled brat like the other selected girls.</b><br /><br />The Selection was not my favorite series. My favorite was definitely <i>The One</i> even though it had many flaws. I couldn't help but rate it a 5 just because it had more improvements and a lot of actual, shocking moments happened. I can see how The Selection came and was born from this, only being told from Queen Amberly's point of view. It's not like America where America doesn't want to enter the Selection and doesn't really care about marrying Prince Maxon, but Amberly has been in love with Clarkson since she was 7 and has wished to marry him, kiss him, have his arms wrapped around her, and yeah all that. Even though The Selection and The Prince are very different, Queen Amberly and America were different when they were selected, it makes sense as to why and how Kiera wrote the series. <br /><br />Queen Amberly has always been the loving and supporting Queen since introduced in the beginning. King Clarkson was known as someone who hardly smiles and pushes everything too hard, too much, and too far. Even though Amberly was the only one to lit his eyes and his world, I can see why he was an asshole. I never liked him, and never wished to try and like him. Luckily I didn't. But I understand why he acted the way he acted in the series and why. He had his reasons, mainly his parents to blame for since they were arguing and both were rude. Even though his mother was rude and would sometimes spoil herself and brag a little because she's Queen, Clarkson was easily able to catch her horrible personality and attitude. <br /><br />Nothing was really new, just made sense to the history of the beloved Amberly and Clarkson Schreave. It was interesting reading this and now I just want to know if Maxon really is Amberly's son. <b>HA. HA. HA!</b> Even though Amberly was told she <i>may or may not be able to have children,</i> there was still a possibility it was wrong. With that, I actually want to know how everything worked out and how Maxon was born. Not in the wrong way, I just want to know if Amberly took medication for this or if treatment was needed. If nothing was wrong, I want to know how it all worked out. Even though nothing was new and everything felt the same, there are still questions I have unanswered, but I guess it doesn't matter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="230480306686904622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12535233609410658248">This is the <b>suckest</b> book I`ve read in a year. It`s only 72 pages long and almost each one of them made me scream internally. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429729620ra/14624999.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>We get a glimpse of the life of Maxon`s parents: Queen Amberly and King Clarkson. Only she`s not a Queen yet and he`s just a Prince, looking for a wife. Amberly is a part of the Selection. She barely knows Clarkson (only thanks to TV) but he was the love of her life since before she could walk. Every night she prayed on his photo and picked names for their future babies. <br/>T</span>
  <span id="freeText12535233609410658248" style="display:none">This is the <b>suckest</b> book I`ve read in a year. It`s only 72 pages long and almost each one of them made me scream internally. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429729620ra/14624999.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We get a glimpse of the life of Maxon`s parents: Queen Amberly and King Clarkson. Only she`s not a Queen yet and he`s just a Prince, looking for a wife. Amberly is a part of the Selection. She barely knows Clarkson (only thanks to TV) but he was the love of her life since before she could walk. Every night she prayed on his photo and picked names for their future babies. <br>The story starts some time after she started to live in a palace as a Selected. Their first interaction with the Prince went somewhat like that:<br><br>-	Cut your hair.<br>-	You don`t like it?<br>-	Meh, I think you`ll look better with a short hair.<br>-	Well, even though I like my long hair, I would go bald if you asked to. <br><br>So, my first expression was that Amberly is a naïve, boneless fool and Clarkson is a son of a bitch (which turned out to be true, but I won`t even start with his mother, this is a complete shit). My expression only grows stronger after he starts to treat her like trash because of her caste, and she continues to see him as God.<br><br><b>
  <i>«You are never to tell anyone what you do. If anyone asks, your family owns a coffee plantation, and you help run it. Be vague and never, ever let on that you do manual labor. Are we clear?”<br>“Yes, Your Highness.”<br>He eyed me a moment longer, as if to reinforce the point. But his command was all I needed. I’d never not do anything he asked me to.»</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429729620ra/14625000.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He`s a controlling jerk who can compete with Mr. Gray with his 50 shades, only without BDSM factor. His parents are constantly fighting and, because he doesn`t want to be like them, he`s looking for a wife that won`t ever say “no” to him. Yay, problem solved, no fighting! A husband everyone`s been dreaming for! <br>His character can be described by one quote:<br><br><b>
  <i>«I’m the prince, and one day I will be king. My word is law.»</i>
</b><br><br>Moreover, Amberly turned out to be infertile. How do you think he should`ve reacted? Obviously not by ignoring her while she felt depressed and needed his help. But everything ends fine – Clarkson doesn`t like kids anyway. <br><br>If you thought The Selection was awful – try this one. Just for fun. Okay, seriously, don`t read it. I was pleased by the first book, but this novel only spoiled everything, especially my opinion about Maxon`s parents. And I thought I liked Queen Amberly. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381635201ra/5123191.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12535233609410658248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_934942664" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/934942664" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394406877p2/2473504.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/934942664?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=young-adult-genre">young-adult-genre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=short-stories-and-novellas">short-stories-and-novellas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=prequel">prequel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=listened-to-audiobook">listened-to-audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer934942664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9045791493755231912"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22054340.The_Queen__The_Selection___0_4_' title='The Queen (The Selection, #0.4) by Kiera Cass' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Queen</a> is a prequel novella in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2987125.Kiera_Cass' title='Kiera Cass' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kiera Cass</a>'s young adult, dystopian series titled: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18735913.The_Selection_Series_Boxed_Set__The_Selection_0_5__1__2_' title='The Selection Series Boxed Set (The Selection 0.5, 1, 2) by Kiera Cass' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Selection Series</a>. This short story features Maxon's father and mother, King Clarkson and Queen Amberly, and includes the story of how they met through their generation's selection process. <br/><br/>I think most readers don't like King Clarkson in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18735913.The_Selection_Series_Boxed_Set__The_Selection_0_5__1__2_' title='The Selection Series Boxed Set (The Selection 0.5, 1, 2) by Kiera Cass' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Selection Series</a>, so I was curious if he would be portrayed any differently during his younger years as prince. <br/><br/>The answer is...<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425437096ra/13889759.gif' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I have to admit though, Ms. Cass was much</span>
  <span id="freeText9045791493755231912" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22054340.The_Queen__The_Selection___0_4_" title="The Queen (The Selection, #0.4) by Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen</a> is a prequel novella in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2987125.Kiera_Cass" title="Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">Kiera Cass</a>'s young adult, dystopian series titled: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18735913.The_Selection_Series_Boxed_Set__The_Selection_0_5__1__2_" title="The Selection Series Boxed Set (The Selection 0.5, 1, 2) by Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">The Selection Series</a>. This short story features Maxon's father and mother, King Clarkson and Queen Amberly, and includes the story of how they met through their generation's selection process. <br><br>I think most readers don't like King Clarkson in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18735913.The_Selection_Series_Boxed_Set__The_Selection_0_5__1__2_" title="The Selection Series Boxed Set (The Selection 0.5, 1, 2) by Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">The Selection Series</a>, so I was curious if he would be portrayed any differently during his younger years as prince. <br><br>The answer is...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425437096ra/13889759.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have to admit though, Ms. Cass was much more subtle in her character development of Clarkson, but his need to control and his hard-handed threats are still shown through his interactions with others in this prequel. The cycle of violence rings loud and clear within the portrait of this royal family, but any suggestion that Clarkson is a victim rang on deaf ears with me. Amberly is the perfect little submissive, which is something I didn't really view her as in the series, but maybe I just forgot. Through Amberly's point of view, the two of them have a very promising future together, and they may very well be just what each other needs. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22054340.The_Queen__The_Selection___0_4_" title="The Queen (The Selection, #0.4) by Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen</a> gives quite a bit of insight into these two characters, and when compared to the series, does a great job of reinforcing the fairytale aspect of Maxon and America's love story. This novella is a wonderful addition to the series and I would recommend it to fans.<br><br><b>My favorite quote:</b><br><i>“But shouldn't there be a least? Shouldn't there be a bare minimum that life should give you?"</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425437096i/13889760.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9045791493755231912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText16191605827559241423" style="display:none">I always like a backstory and reading about characters or things that have only been touched upon in the main series and this was a nice little additive and insight into a Selection process prior to the one we know in the main books. <br /><br />It was nice to see how Queen Amberley faired in her own selection and a glimpse into her character before she was the Queen although I’m glad this was a separate entity from the books as it does maintain the Queens character as a force to be reckoned with and in this she was vulnerable and fairly weak so it was interesting to see how she had grown from that. And her burgeoning relationship to Clarkson was a nice behind the scenes and feel like I can go into the second book now with an added bit of extra knowledge and backstory. <br /><br />Love this series so far so was happy to read an extra to the main books!</span>

<div id="review_3352509359" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3352509359" />
    <a title="Phoenix Olivia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/93552756-phoenix-olivia"><img alt="Phoenix Olivia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601950386p2/93552756.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3352509359?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phoenix Olivia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phoenix Olivia " href="/user/show/93552756-phoenix-olivia">Phoenix Olivia </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3352509359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4736031647902623637">I enjoyed this book very much. It was so so short. Only around 80 pages long. That was so quick to read but anyways that's not the point. It was fascinating to hear about Queen Amberly and King Clarkson and how they came to be. But I am also wondering why their relationship turned to pieces in the future? I was led to believe that Clarkson was an evil King. He hit Maxon and he had all those marks on his back. And he also had a mistress. I think that's what it's called and he even got her pregnan</span>
  <span id="freeText4736031647902623637" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book very much. It was so so short. Only around 80 pages long. That was so quick to read but anyways that's not the point. It was fascinating to hear about Queen Amberly and King Clarkson and how they came to be. But I am also wondering why their relationship turned to pieces in the future? I was led to believe that Clarkson was an evil King. He hit Maxon and he had all those marks on his back. And he also had a mistress. I think that's what it's called and he even got her pregnant. So if he loved Amberly why would he do something like that? I guess he turned out to be more like his dad after all but it's sad knowing they once had something wonderful and it all changed. I would have enjoyed reading what their marriage was like in the future. I think that would be quite interesting.</span>

  <span id="freeText17000221867530289820" style="display:none">“It’s a strange thing to discover how much you matter to people you didn’t really know you mattered to.”<br /><br />I didn’t know how to read this series, so I decided to read novellas before, I don’t know if it is the right sequence…Well, there are a lot of characters in the story, maybe I’ll understand everyone after reading book 1.<br /><br />Amberly who is a simple girl from a world where people are divided in a caste system number wise, where there is a selection process going on for selection of next queen and every girl from any caste can participate.<br /><br />“On the contrary, he was a mystery I was excited to solve.” <br /><br />Amberly is in love with the prince from her childhood, but she is from a low caste with health issues. There were only 72 pages though, I really enjoyed reading it.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2075416404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14505901988626298386">Another one of The Selection series? A book on Queen Amberly? Yes please!<br/><br/>The Queen is the story of Queen Amberly, a glimpse of her life while she was competing in the selection for Prince Clarkson’s hand. We get to see her life, her family and the real Amberly beneath all the façade of grandiose we saw of her in The Selection. <br/><br/>It was plainly obvious that Amberly was going to be the queen but it still was delightful to read of how she came to the throne. Prince Clarkson doesn’t seem as bad as he </span>
  <span id="freeText14505901988626298386" style="display:none">Another one of The Selection series? A book on Queen Amberly? Yes please!<br /><br />The Queen is the story of Queen Amberly, a glimpse of her life while she was competing in the selection for Prince Clarkson’s hand. We get to see her life, her family and the real Amberly beneath all the façade of grandiose we saw of her in The Selection. <br /><br />It was plainly obvious that Amberly was going to be the queen but it still was delightful to read of how she came to the throne. Prince Clarkson doesn’t seem as bad as he was, as a king. But his thirst for power and his desire to have control is obvious here too, even though the impact is slightly lessened while seeing it through the rose-colored eyes of Amberly. <br /><br />Eitherway, this was fun and delightful :)</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PlKhsJMiAEDbQu03fqUwHSa51sX9s1382UcnBURIIf1xyWwMMGQP2mAPCHrFXqsc/LMK7rNnlGfZzD9+6F4dtA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xk9i0Nz9cWG+i6h8bUgdoKiRCQK5KTtaWKmnsj/ZzWKJ1K9sf7t++wXGTTHWs4ahcpvVKff98sFYIr/Jk8/xKw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Stickers. School Spirit. My friends. Living in a small town. Japan. Singing. Painting my toenails. Pranks/ practical jokes. Painting. Stretch canvas. Costumes. Dipping my fingers in melted wax. Style. Soda. Spending an hour typing at a coffee shop. Musicals. Back to school season. Mopeds. Good hair days. Naps. Not walking up but looking at a beautiful staircase. Driving alone. My ankles. Playlists. Spending entire days in pajamas. Holidays. Telling stories. Spontaneity. Theme parks. Bookshelves. The word copacetic. Boxes. Empty journals. Surprises. Doing things in groups. Doing things alone. Getting real mail. Decorating. Small forks. A good hug. Gift cards. New Years Goals. Going out to dinner. When someone else remembers some great story about me/us that I’ve forgotten. Toy stores. Fireplaces. Breakfast foods. Journaling. Crying for a good reason. Doorbells. Pointless adventures. Voting. My birthday. Reasons to make wishes. Recycling.<br /></span>
